CITY OF BOISE CITY, IDAHO
$76,835,000 Water Renewal Revenue & Refunding Bonds, Series 2022 
DATED: Date of Delivery (estimated to be June 30, 2022)      DUE: September 1, as shown herein
The City of Boise City, Idaho Water Renewal Revenue & Refunding Bonds, Series 2022 (the “Series 2022 Bonds”) will 
be issued by the City of Boise City, Idaho (the “City”) pursuant to Ordinance No. ORD-24-22 adopted by the City on 
May 17, 2022, as supplemented and amended (the “Master Ordinance”), and Ordinance No. ORD-25-22 adopted by the 
City on May 17, 2022 (the “Series 2022 Ordinance” and together with the Master Ordinance, collectively, the “Bond 
Ordinance”). The Series 2022 Bonds are being issued to (i) currently refund certain of the City’s Water Renewal 
Revenue Refunding Bonds, Series 2012 (the “Refunded Bonds”), (ii) finance the acquisition and construction of certain 
improvements to the City’s Water Renewal System (the “Project”), and (iii) pay the costs of issuance of the Series 2022 
Bonds.
The Series 2022 Bonds are initially issuable in book-entry form only through The Depository Trust Company, New 
York, New York (“DTC”), which will act as securities depository for the Series 2022 Bonds.  The Series 2022 Bonds bear 
interest payable semiannually on each March 1 and September 1, beginning March 1, 2023 to the maturity of the Series 
2022 Bonds.  Principal will be payable annually each September 1 as indicated herein, beginning September 1, 2023 to the 
maturity of the Series 2022 Bonds. See “Maturity Schedule” on inside cover hereof.  The Series 2022 Bonds are subject to 
redemption prior to their stated maturities as further described herein. See “Redemption Provisions” herein. 
The Series 2022 Bonds are secured by a pledge of the Net Revenue of the System (hereinafter defined) superior 
to all other charges of any kind.  The City reserves the right to issue parity bonds secured by a pledge of the Net 
Revenues upon compliance with certain conditions.  THE SERIES 2022 BONDS ARE SPECIAL OBLIGATIONS 
OF THE CITY PAYABLE ONLY FROM THE BOND FUND. THE SERIES 2022 BONDS DO NOT CONSTITUTE 
GENERAL OBLIGATIONS OF THE CITY OR THE STATE OF IDAHO (THE “STATE”), OR ANY POLITICAL 
SUBDIVISION OF THE STATE, OR A CHARGE UPON ANY GENERAL FUND OR UPON ANY MONEY OR 
OTHER PROPERTY OF THE CITY OR OF THE STATE, OR OF ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION OF THE 
STATE NOT SPECIFICALLY PLEDGED BY THE CITY’S BOND ORDINANCE AUTHORIZING THE SERIES 
2022 BONDS. NEITHER THE FULL FAITH AND CREDIT NOR THE TAXING POWER OF THE CITY, STATE 
OF IDAHO, NOR ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION THEREOF, IS PLEDGED FOR PAYMENT OF THE SERIES 
2022 BONDS. See “SECURITY FOR THE SERIES 2022 BONDS.”
MATURITY SCHEDULE—ON INSIDE COVER
The Series 2022 Bonds are offered when, as and if received and accepted by BofA Securities, subject to the final approving 
legal opinion of Bond Counsel.  Certain matters will be passed on for the City by the City Attorney and by its disclosure 
counsel, Hawley Troxell Ennis & Hawley LLP. Certain matters will be passed on for the Underwriter by its legal counsel, 
Hawkins Delafield & Wood LLP. It is expected that the Series 2022 Bonds will be available for delivery to the Bond 
Registrar on behalf of DTC by Fast Automated Securities Transfer on or about June 30, 2022 (the “Date of Delivery”).
This cover page contains certain information for quick reference only. It is not a summary of the issue.  Investors 
must read the entire Official Statement to obtain information essential to the making of an informed investment 
decision.

 OFFICIAL STATEMENT 
City of Boise City, Idaho 
$76,835,000 Water Renewal Revenue & Refunding Bonds, Series 2022   
The City of Boise, Idaho (the “City”), a municipal corporation duly organized and existing under and by virtue of the laws 
of the State of Idaho (the “State”), furnishes this Official Statement in connection with the offering of its $76,835,000 
aggregate principal amount of Water Renewal Revenue & Refunding Bonds , Series 2022 (the “Series 2022 Bonds”), 
dated the date of delivery. Certain capitalized words and phrases used in this Official Statement and not defined herein 
have the meanings as defined in the Bond Ordinance (hereinafter defined), which is attached hereto as “Appendix B.” 
The Series 2022 Bonds are being issued to (i) currently refund certain of the City’s Water Renewal Revenue Refunding 
Bonds, Series 2012 (the “Refunded Bonds”), (ii) finance the acquisition and construction of certain improvements to the 
City’s Water Renewal System  (the “Project”), and (iii) pay the costs of issuance of the Series 2022 Bonds.  See 
“DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS – Authorization for Issuance” and “PURPOSE AND USE OF PROCEEDS.” The 
defeasance and redemption of the Refunded Bonds is referred to herein as the “Refunding Plan.” See “PURPOSE AND USE 
OF PROCEEDS – Refunding Plan.” 
The Refunded Bonds were issued to refinance certain capital improvements to the City’s Water Renewal (Sewer) Utility 
System (the “System”). See “T HE SYSTEM” herein for further detail. The City has reserved the right in the Master 
Ordinance (hereafter defined) to issue additional bonds or obligations with a lien on Net Revenues (as defined below) of 
the System on a parity with the lien on the Series 2022 Bonds upon satisfaction of certain conditions  (“Parity Bonds”).  
See “SECURITY FOR THE SERIES 2022 BONDS–Future Obligations–Parity Bonds.”  The Series 2022 Bonds and any Parity 
Bonds are hereinafter collectively referred to as the “Bonds.” 
The Series 2022 Bonds are revenue obligations of the System.  Neither the full faith and credit nor the taxing power of 
the City is pledged to the payment of the Series 2022 Bonds.  The Series 2022 Bonds are not obligations of the State or 
any political subdivision thereof other than the City.  See “SECURITY FOR THE SERIES 2022 BONDS.” 
This Official Statement, which includes the cover page and appendices, provides information concerning the City, the 
Series 2022 Bonds and the System.   
The information set forth herein has been obtained from the City and other sources that are believed to be reliable.  BofA 
Securities, Inc. (the “Underwriter”) has relied on the City with respect to the accuracy and sufficiency of such information, 
and such information is not to be construed as a representation, warranty or guarantee by the Underwriter.  So far as any 
statement herein includes matters of opinion, or estimates of future expenses and income, whether or not expressly so 
stated, they are intended merely as such and not as representations of fact. 
DESCRIPTION OF THE SERIES 2022 BONDS 
Authorization for Issuance 
The Series 2022 Bonds are issued pursuant to Ordinance No. ORD-24-22 adopted by the City on May 17, 2022, as it may 
be supplemented and amended (the “Master Ordinance”), and Ordinance No. ORD-25-22 adopted by the City on May 
17, 2022 (the “Series 2022 Ordinance” and together with the Master Ordinance, collectively the “Bond Ordinance”), and 
under and in accordance with the City Code and the laws and provisions of the State, including Idaho Code Sections 50-
1027 through 50-1042, inclusive, and chapter 2, Title 57, Idaho Code (collectively, the “Act”).  
A ballot measure allowing the City to issue revenue bonds in the aggregate amount of up to $570 million over the next 
ten years (the “Bonding Capacity”) was approved by a favorable vote at an election held in the City on November 2, 2021. 
The City can issue the Bonding Capacity in one or more series  of revenue bonds or through other obligations. The  
 2 
Refunded Bonds were issued pursuant to Resolution No. 21820, adopted by the City on August 14, 2012, for the purpose 
of financing improvements to the System.  Refundings of outstanding revenue bonds may be issued without a vote of the 
electorate of the City  and such par amounts allocated to r efunding bonds are not considered when determining the 
remaining Bonding Capacity. Nothing in the Bond Ordinance prevents the City from seeking authority to increase the 
Bonding Capacity at subsequent bond elections or by means of judicial confirmation under Idaho Code, Title 7, Chapter 
13.  
Principal Amount, Date, Interest Rates and Maturities 
The Series 2022 Bonds will be issued in the principal amounts shown on the inside cover page of this Official Statement 
and will be dated and bear interest from the Date of Delivery.  The Series 2022 Bonds will mature on the dates set forth 
on the inside cover page of this Official Statement and will bear interest, payable semiannually, until the maturity or 
earlier redemption of the Series 2022 Bonds.  Interest on the Series 2022 Bonds will be computed on the basis of a 360-
day year consisting of twelve 30-day months.   
Redemption Provisions 
Optional Redemption. The Series 2022 Bonds maturing on and before September 1, 2032, are not subject to redemption 
prior to maturity.  The Series 2022 Bonds maturing on and after September 1, 2033, are subject to redemption at the option 
of the City, in whole or in part on September 1, 2032, and any date thereafter at the price of par plus accrued interest, if 
any, to the date of redemption. 
Mandatory Sinking Fund Redemption.  The Series 2022 Bonds maturing on September 1, 2047 are subject to mandatory 
sinking fund redemption prior to their stated maturity, at a price of 100% of the principal amount of the Series 2022 Bonds 
to be so redeemed, plus accrued interest to the date fixed for redemption, on September 1 of the years, and in the amounts, 
shown below:

 3 
Selection for Redemption. For as long as the Series 2022 Bonds are in book-entry only form, if fewer than all of the Series 
2022 Bonds are called for redemption, the selection of Series 2022 Bonds to be redeemed will be made by The Depository 
Trust Company, New York, New York (“DTC”) in accordance with its operational procedures then in effect.  If less than 
all of a Series 2022 Bond that is subject to mandatory sinking fund redemption is to be redeemed, the redemption price 
shall be applied to such mandatory sinking fund installments as the City shall direct. See Appendix E attached hereto.  If 
the Series 2022 Bonds are no longer held in book-entry only form, then Zions Bancorporation, National Association, as 
the bond registrar and paying agent (the “Bond Registrar ”), will select Series 2022 Bonds for redemption by lot in 
multiples of $5,000 within each maturity. 
Notice of Redemption (Book-Entry). So long as the Series 2022 Bonds are in book-entry only form, the Bond Registrar 
will notify DTC of an early redemption not less than 30 days prior to the date fixed for redemption, and will provide such 
information as required by a letter of representation submitted to DTC in connection with the issuance of the Series 2022 
Bonds. 
Notice of Redemption (No Book -Entry). During any period in which the Series 2022 Bonds are not in book-entry only 
form, unless waived by any person in whose name such Bonds are registered (the “Beneficial Owners”) of the Series 2022 
Bonds to be redeemed, official notice of any redemption of Bonds will be given by the Bond Registrar on behalf of the 
City by mailing a copy of an official redemption notice by first class mail, postage prepaid, no less than 30 days and not 
more than 60 days prior to the date fixed for redemption, to the Beneficial Owners of the Series 2022 Bonds to be redeemed 
at the address shown on the bond register or at such other address as is furnished in writing by such Beneficial Owner to 
the Bond Registrar. 
Conditional Notice of Redemp tion. Any notice of optional redemption given for the Series 2022 Bonds pursuant to the 
Series 2022 Ordinance may state that the optional redemption is conditional upon receipt by the Bond Registrar of amounts 
sufficient to pay the redemption price of such Series 2022 Bonds or upon the satisfaction of any other condition, and/or 
that such notice may be rescinded upon the occurrence of any other event, and any conditional notice so given may be 
rescinded at any time before payment of such redemption price if any such condition so specified is not satisfied or if any 
such other event occurs. Notice of such rescission or of the failure of any such condition shall be given by the Bond 
Registrar to affected owners of the Series 2022 Bonds as promptly as practicable. 
Defeasance 
In the event that money and/or “government obligations,” as defined in Idaho Code Section 57-504, as it may be amended, 
maturing at such time or times and bearing interest to be earned thereon in amounts sufficient to redeem and retire the 
Series 2022 Bonds or any of them in accordance with their terms are irrevocably deposited with an escrow agent to effect 
such redemption, then no further payments need be made into the Bond Fund under the Bond Ordinance for the payment 
of the principal of and interest on the Series 2022 Bonds so provided for. Such Bonds will cease to be entitled to any lien, 
benefit or security of the Bond Ordinance except the right to receive the funds so set aside and pledged, and such  Bonds 
will be deemed not to be outstanding.  
Bond Registrar and Registration Features 
Book-Entry System.  The Series 2022 Bonds will be issued in fully registered form and, when issued, will be registered in 
the name of Cede & Co. as Bond Owner and as nom inee for DTC.  DTC will act as securities depository for the Series 
2022 Bonds.  Individual purchases and sales of the Series 2022 Bonds may be made in book-entry form only in minimum 
denominations of $5,000 and integral multiples thereof.  Purchasers will not receive certificates representing their interest 
in the Series 2022 Bonds.  See “Appendix E—Book Entry Only System” attached hereto for additional information. 
Bond Registrar.  The principal of and interest on the Series 2022 Bonds will be payable by the Bond Registrar to DTC, 
which, in turn, is obligated to remit such principal and interest to its participants (“DTC Participants”) for subsequent 
disbursement to the Beneficial Owners of the Series 2022 Bonds, as further described in “Appendix E—Book Entry Only 
System” attached hereto.  Interest on the Series 2022 Bonds  will be credited to the Beneficial Owners by the DTC 
Participants.   
 4 
Procedure in the Event of Revisions of Book-Entry Transfer System. If DTC resigns as the securities depository and the 
City is unable to retain a qualified successor to DTC, or the City has determined that it is in the best interest of the City 
not to continue the book-entry system of transfer or that interests of the Beneficial Owners of the Series 2022 Bonds might 
be adversely affected if the book -entry system of transfer is continued, the City will execute, authenticate and deliver at 
no cost to the Beneficial Owners of the Series 2022 Bonds  or their nominees, Bonds in fully r egistered form, in the 
denomination of $5,000 or any integral multiple thereof.  Thereafter, the principal of the Series 2022 Bonds will be payable 
upon due presentment and surrender thereof at the principal office of the Bond Registrar ; interest on the Series 2022 
Bonds will be mailed or caused to be delivered to the persons in whose names such Bonds are registered, at the address 
appearing upon the registration books on the fifteenth day preceding the interest payment date, or, if not a business day  
for the Bond Registrar, the next preceding day that is a business day for the Bond Registrar, and the Series 2022 Bonds 
will be transferable as provided in the Bond Ordinance. 
Litigation 
There is no litigation pending questioning the validity of the Series 2022 Bonds nor the power and authority of the City 
to issue the Series 2022 Bonds.  There is no litigation pending that would materially affect the Revenue of the System or 
affect the City’s ability to meet debt service requirements on the Series 2022 Bonds.  
PURPOSE AND USE OF PROCEEDS 
Purpose 
The proceeds from the sale of the Series 2022 Bonds will be used to (i) currently refund the outstanding principal amount 
of the Refunded Bonds,  (ii) finance the Project, as defined below, and (iii) pay the costs of issuance of the Series 2022 
Bonds. 
Refunding Plan 
Pursuant to an escrow agreement dated the date of delivery of the Series 2022 Bonds between Zions Bancorporation, 
National Association, serving in its role as escrow agent for the Refunded Bonds (the “Escrow Agent”) and the City (the 
“Escrow Agreement”), a portion of the proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds will purchase certain direct United States 
government obligations (“Government Obligations”) to be deposited into the City of Boise City, Wastewater Facility 
Refunding Bond, Series 2012 Escrow Fund (the “Escrow Fund”), together with a cash deposit, for the purpose of defeasing 
and refunding the outstanding principal amount of the Refunded Bonds, plus accrued interest to the date of redemption, 
all in accordance with the Escrow Agreement.  See “S
OURCES AND USES OF FUNDS.”  
The Refunded Bonds were privately placed and do not have a CUSIP number. 
Escrow Fund. The Government Obligations, interest earned thereon, and necessary cash balance will be irrevocably 
pledged to and held in trust by the Escrow Agent in the Escrow Fund for the benefit of the owners of the Refunded Bonds. 
In the opinion of Bond Counsel, the Refunded Bonds will be legally defeased as of the issue date of the Series 2022 Bonds 
and such defeasance will not adversely affect the exclusion of interest on the Refunded Bonds from gross income for 
federal income tax purposes.  
Verification of Mathematical Calculations. Samuel Klein and Company, Certified Public Accountants, will deliver to the 
City on or before the issue date of the Series 2022 Bonds, its verification re port indicating that it has verified the 
mathematical accuracy of the mathematical computations of the adequacy of the cash and the maturing principal of and 
interest on the Government Obligations, to pay, when due, all of the principal of and interest on the Refunded Bonds to 
and including to the date of redemption.    
 5 
Project 
A portion of the proceeds from the sale of the Series 2022 Bonds will be used to finance a portion of certain capital 
improvements to the System (the “Project”) designed to address aging infrastructure, treatment capacity needs, increased 
regulatory requirements, climate change, and water supply resiliency. The Project will occur in phases over the next ten 
years. The Project is broken into four programs:    
Lander Street Water Renewal Facility (“WRF”) Program: Includes upgrades to address capacity limitations, 
current and future regulatory compliance (e.g. phosphorus, ammonia, biological oxygen demand, and suspended 
solids removal), and aging infrastructure by constructing new tertiary filtration, replacing primary clarifiers, and 
expanding secondary treatment capacity.
 
West Boise WRF Program: Addresses capacity limitations, regulatory compliance, and aging infrastructure by 
expanding secondary treatment capacity and constr ucting ultraviolet disinfection improvements, new tertiary 
treatment, and communications center. Improvements will achieve redundancy requirements and enhance effluent 
water quality by meeting increasingly stringent requirements.
 
Recycled Water Program: Includes construction of a new, third WRF to renew approximately 5 million gallons 
per day (“mgd”) of industrial flows for commercial and industrial reuse and aquifer recharge, and a recycled water 
distribution system (booster stations, storage tanks, and distribution and transmission mains). The Recycled Water 
Program will create drought-proof water supplies to support industrial and commercial growth in rapidly expanding 
southeast Boise. The new, third WRF will also enable the C ity to achieve regulatory requirements for total 
phosphorus and temperature by diverting effluent from the Boise River and replenish local aquifers suffering from 
water supply challenges.  
Collections and Conveyance Pro gram: Includes rehabilitation, repair, or replacement of aging, high -risk 
infrastructure such as pipelines, lift stations, and diversions. These improvements will protect water quality, 
improve system reliability, and eliminate costly failures. 
Additional Funding for Project. The overall cost of the Project is currently estimated at approximately $815 million, 
which the City intends to fund with a combination of rate-funded revenue of the System  (“Rate-Funded Capital”), the 
proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds, and additional future borrowings.  See “T
HE SYSTEM – Capital Improvement Plan” 
below. In July 2021, t he City submitted a letter of interest to the Water Infrastructure Finance and Innovation Act 
(“WIFIA”) program, which is a federal project administered by the United States Environmental Protection Agency (the 
“EPA”). The City was selected to submit an application, which indicates the EPA’s intent to fund, following the 
application submittal and negotiation of terms. The City is currently applying for funding and anticipates receiving a loan 
in the amount of approximately $399 million from the EPA under the WIFIA program (the “WIFIA Loan”) to finance a 
portion of the Project.  The City expects to issue the WIFIA Loan as a Parity Bond under the Master Ordinance. The City 
anticipates the WIFIA Loan would close in Fiscal Year 2023, be structured as a draw-down loan and be drawn down by 
Fiscal Year 2032 . The final maturity of the WIFIA Loan would be 30 years after the loan takeout and substantial 
completion of the Project. The details and expectations surrounding the WIFIA Loan are preliminary and subject to 
change.

SECURITY FOR THE SERIES 2022 BONDS 
Pledge of Net Revenues  
The Series 2022 Bonds are revenue obligations payable from and secured by a pledge of the Revenue of the System after 
deduction of Operation and Maintenance Expenses (the “Net Revenues”) .  Revenue of the System includes all earnings, 
revenue and moneys received by the City from or on account of the operation of the System  under generally accepted 
accounting principles, including income from investments of money in the Bond Fund (hereinafter defined)  or from any 
other investment thereof, except the income from investments irrevocably pledged to the payment of any other reve nue 
obligations of the City pursuant to a plan of retirement or refunding. Revenue  shall be increased and/or decreased in 
accordance with the Master Ordinance. Specific items excluded from Revenue can be found in the Master Ordinance. See 
“Appendix B—Master Bond Ordinance and Series 2022 Ordinance.” Operation and Maintenance Expenses of the System 
include all costs incurred by the City and properly treated as expenses of operating, maintaining and repairing the System 
under generally accepted accounting principles, whether paid or accrued, or of levying, collecting and otherwise 
administering the Revenue of the System for the payment of the Bonds, including but not limited to those expenses further 
enumerated in the Master Ordinance, but not including any payment for debt service or deposits into a reserve account, 
depreciation or taxes levied or imposed by the City of payments to the City in lieu of taxes, or capital additions or capital 
replacements to the System. See “Appendix B—Master Bond Ordinance and Series 2022 Ordinance.” 
The Series 2022 Bonds  constitute a lien and charge on the Net Revenues prior and superior to any other charges 
whatsoever except that the lien and charge may be on a parity with any Parity Bonds that the City may issue in the future. 
The Series 2022 Bonds are special fund obligations of the City payable only from amounts on deposit in the Bond Fund, 
which includes the Debt Service Account and Debt Service Reserve Account, if funded, and any subaccounts thereunder. 
See “Water Renewal Services Funds and Accounts” below. The Bond Fund will at all times be completely segregated and 
set apart from all other funds and accounts of the City for the security and the payment of the principal of and interest on 
the Series 2022 Bonds as they become due. The Series 2022 Bonds are not an obligation of the State, Ada County (the 
“County”) or any political subdivision thereof other than the City, and neither the full faith and credit nor the taxing power 
of the City, the County or the State are pledged to the payment of the Series 2022 Bonds.  
 7 
Rate Covenant 
The City has established and has covenanted in the Bond Ordinance to maintain and collect from the users of the System, 
rates and charges for furnishing the services and the facilities of the System to such users thereof. The City has covenanted 
to establish, maintain and collect such rates and charges for service of its System to satisfy the Rate Covenant for so long 
as any Bonds are Outstanding. The “Rate Covenant” requires Net Revenue in each Fiscal Year at least equal to 125% of 
the amount of principal and interest required to be paid in such Fiscal Year on all Outstanding Bonds, as adjusted in 
accordance with the Master Ordinance. See “THE SYSTEM” below for historical Net Revenues and Debt Service Coverage, 
as well as projected Net Revenues and Debt Service Coverage.  
Water Renewal Services Funds and Accounts 
The Bond Ordinance created the following funds and accounts, that will be held and administered by the City: the City of 
Boise Water Renewal Revenue Fund (the “Revenue Fund”), including the Stabilization Account therein, the City of Boise 
Water Renewal Revenue Bond Fund (the “Bond Fund”), including the Debt Service Account and Debt Service Reserve 
Account therein (the “Reserve Account”), the City of Boise Water Renewal Revenue Project Fund (the “Project Fund”), 
and the Rebate Fund (collectively, the “Funds”). Additional information o n each of these Funds follows. See “P URPOSE 
AND USE OF PROCEEDS – Refunding Plan” above for information related to the Escrow Fund. 
Revenue Fund. Pursuant to the Master Ordinance the City is required to maintain the Revenue Fund as a separate enterprise 
fund of the City, and to deposit the Revenue of the System into the Revenue Fund as collected. The Revenue of the System 
shall be used for payment of the following obligations in the following order of priority: 
(1) to pay the Operation and Maintenance Expenses of the System;  
(2) to pay the interest on any Bonds; 
(3) to pay the principal of Bonds; 
(4) to make all payments required to be made into the Reserve Account, and any subaccounts thereunder , 
created in the future for the payment of debt service on any series of Bonds; 
(5) to make all payments, together with other available funds, on the day on which any rebates or penalties 
for Bonds are due to be paid to the United States pursuant to Section 148 of the Code;  
(6) to make all payments required to be made into a revenue bond redemption fund or revenue warrant 
redemption fund and debt service fund or reserve account hereafter created to pay and secure the payment 
of the principal of and interest on any loans or bonds which have a lien upon the Net Revenues of the 
System junior and inferior to the lien thereon for the payment of the principal of and interest on the Bonds; 
and 
(7) to retire by redemption or purchase any outstanding Bonds or subordinate revenue warrants or subordinate 
Bonds of the City payable out of the Net Revenues of the System, to make necessary additions, 
betterments, improvements and repairs to or extensions and replacements of the System, or for any other 
lawful City purposes. 
Upon satisfaction of the obligations above, the City may use Revenue of the System for any other lawful purpose, 
including but not limited to capital improvements. See “T
HE SYSTEM–Capital Improvement Plan.” 
Stabilization Account. The City has created a Stabilization Account in the Revenue Fund pursuant to the Master 
Ordinance, and shall maintain that account as long as Bonds are Outstanding. Net Revenues may be transferred 
to the Stabilization Account at the option of the City on any date. Money in the Stabilization Account may be 
withdrawn at any time and used for an y purpose for which the Revenue  may be used.  Any deposits to or 
withdrawals from the Stabilization Account will decrease or increase, respectively, Revenue in the Fiscal Year 
for which such deposit or withdrawal was made. The City may ad just any deposits to and withdrawa ls from the 
Stabilization Account for up to 180 days after the close of the applicable Fiscal Year. The City will fund the 
Stabilization Account in the amount of $5 million at settlement of the Series 2022 Bonds.   
 8 
Bond Fund. The Bond Fund exists solely for  the purpose of paying the principal of, premium, if any, and interest on the 
Bonds. The Bond Fund consists of two accounts known as the “Debt Service Account” and the “Debt Service Reserve 
Account,” (the “Reserve Account”), and any subaccounts thereunder, as more fully described below: 
Debt Service Account. As long as any Bonds rem ain Outstanding, the City is required by the Master Ordinance 
to set aside and pay from the Revenue Fund into the Debt Service Account those amounts necessary, together 
with such other funds as are on hand and available in the Debt Service Account, to pay the principal of and interest 
next coming due on the Bonds. Pursuant to the Series 2022 Ordinance, the City established the “Series 2022 Debt 
Service Account,” a subaccount to be held by the City for the payment the Series 2022 Bonds.  
Reserve Account. The M aster Ordinance requires the City to maintain a Reserve Account, and any subaccounts 
established thereunder, if required by  any series ordinance for the purpose of securing the payment of principal 
of an d interest on the respective Bonds subject to a Reserve Account Requirement, as defined in the Master 
Ordinance. The Series 2022 Ordinance did not establish a subaccount thereunder and the Series 2022 Bonds are 
not secured by the Reserve Account and not subject to a Reserve Account Requirement. 
Moneys in the various accounts within the Bond Fund may be invested in Permitted Investments. Investments of funds in 
the 
accounts within the Bond Fund shall mature prior to the date on which such moneys shall be needed for required 
interest, principal, or sinking fund installments. Investments of funds in the Reserve Account shall be available to pay any 
deficiencies that may occur in any of the accounts within the Bond Fund. All interest earned and income derived by virtue 
of such investments shall remain in the Bond Fund and be used to meet the required deposits into any account therein. 
Subject to the other provisions of the Bond Ordinance, moneys in the Debt Service Account and the Reserve Account 
may be combined for the purpose of purchasing investments, but the records of the City shall show to which account the 
respective portions of any such combined investment are credited. 
Project Fund. The Master Ordinance creates the Project Fund, whereby a portion of the proceeds of the Bonds shall be 
deposited for the payment of the cost of acquisition and construction of improvements to the System, including costs of 
issuance of the Bonds.  The Series 2022 Ordinance established the “Series 2022 Project Account” to be held by the City 
and used to pay the Cost of Acquisition and Construction of the Project and costs of issuance of the Series 2022 Bonds. 
Any moneys remaining in the Series 2022 Project Account after the full and final payment of the costs of the Project shall 
be transferred to the City and deposited in the Debt Service Account.  
Rebate Fund.  A Rebate Fund is established under the Master Ordinance into which shall be deposited, from time to time, 
all excess earnings on funds and accounts held by the City pursuant to the Master Ordinance or any series ordinance,  to 
the extent required by any Tax Certificate of the City and said amounts shall be held in trust for the payment of arbitrage 
rebate in accordance with Section 148 of the Code and the Tax Certificate.  All earnings on the Rebate Fund shall remain 
within said fund and shall be used for  no other purpose unless the City provides the Bond Registrar with an opinion of 
nationally recognized bond counsel that another use will not cause interest on the respective Bonds to cease to qualify for 
exclusion from federal income taxation under the Code. 
Future Obligations  
Parity Bonds. The City reserves the right in the Master Ordinance to issue Parity Bonds, which will constitute a lien and 
charge on the Net Revenues of the System on a parity with the Series 2022 Bonds, but only if (a) no Event of Default (as 
defined in the Master Ordinance) under the Master Ordinance or any Series Ordinance has occurred and is continuing; 
and (b) a t the time of issuance of the Parity Bonds there is no deficiency in the Debt Service Account and all required 
deposits to all subaccounts, if any, in the Reserve Account have been made.  
The Master Ordinance also requires that there be filed with the City either:  
(1) A certificate of the Director of Finance and Administration or the Deputy City Treasurer stating that Net 
Revenues, adjusted as hereafter described, for (i) any twelve consecutive months selected by the City or Qualified 
Consultant out of the most recent eighteen months preceding the delivery of the Parity Bonds or (ii) the most  
 9 
recently completed Fiscal Year for which audited financial statements are available (the “Base Period”), were not 
less than one hundred twenty five percent (125%) of Maximum Annual Debt Service on all then O utstanding 
Bonds, calculated as of the date the Parity Bonds are issued and with the proposed Parity Bonds treated as 
Outstanding. The City may adjust Net Revenues for purposes of this paragraph (1) by adding any Net Revenues 
the Director of Finance and Administration or the Deputy City Treasurer calculates the City would have had in 
the Revenue Fund during the Base Period because of increases in System rates, fees and charges which have been 
adopted by the City and are in effect on or before the date the Parity Bonds are issued. The City shall adjust Net 
Revenues for the Base Period by eliminating the effect of any withdrawals from or deposits to the  Stabilization 
Account; or 
 
(2) A certificate or opinion of a Qualified Consultant: (i) Stating the amount of the “Adjusted Net Revenues” for each 
of the five Fiscal Years after the last Fiscal Year for which interest on the Parity Bonds is, or is expected to be, 
capitalized, or, if interest will not be capitalized, for each of the five (5) Fiscal Years after the proposed Parity 
Bonds are issued; and (ii) concluding the respective amounts of Adjusted Net Revenues in each of the first four 
Fiscal Years described in this paragraph (2)(i) above are at least equal to one hundred twenty-five percent (125%) 
of the Annual Bond Debt Service for each of those respective Fiscal Years on all Outstanding Bonds, with the 
proposed Parity Bonds treated as Outstanding; and (iii) concluding the amount of Adjusted Net Revenues in the 
fifth Fiscal Year described in this paragraph (2)(i) above is at least equal to one hundred twenty-five percent 
(125%) of the Maximum Annual Debt Service, calculated for the period beginning with that fifth Fiscal Year on 
all then Outstanding Bonds, with the proposed Parity Bonds treated as Outstanding.  The Qualified Consultant 
shall calculate “Adjusted Net Revenues” for purposes of this paragraph (2)(i) as set forth in Section 14(e) of the 
Master Ordinance.  
Refunding Bonds . If the Parity Bonds are being issued for the purpose of refunding Outstanding Bonds  (“Refunding 
Bonds”), the City may do so without complying with the requirements of “Parity Bonds” above , so long as the refunded 
Bonds are legally or economically defeased on the date of delivery of the Refunding Bonds and if the Annual Bond Debt 
Service on the Refunding Bonds does not exceed the Annual Bond Debt Service on the refunded Bonds in any Fiscal 
Year by more than five percent (5%).  
Subordinate Obligations . Nothing in the Bond Ordinance shall prevent the City from issuing revenue bonds or other 
obligations which are a charge upon the Net Revenues of the System subordinate to the lien of the Bonds (“Subordinate 
Obligations”). As of the date hereof, the City has no Subordinate Obligations.   
Separate Utility System 
Pursuant to the Master Ordinance, the City may declare property that the City owns and is part of the System, but that has 
a value of less than ten percent (10%) of the System at the time of such declaration, and property which the City has not 
yet acquired but would otherwise become part of the System, to be part of a “Separate Utility System.” A Separate Utility 
System means any water supply, sewage collection or treatment, stormwater or other utility service or facilities that may 
be created, acquired or constructed by the City in accordance with the Master Ordinance. 
The City may pay costs of acquiring, operating and maintaining a Separate Utility System from Net Revenues, but only 
if there is no deficit in the Debt Service Account or Reserve Account within the Bond Fund. The City may issue obligations 
which are secured by the revenues produced by the Separate Utility System and may pledge the Separate Utility System 
revenues to pay those obligations. In addition, the City may i ssue Subordinate Obligations to pay for costs of a Separate 
Utility System and may pledge the revenues of the Separate Utility System to pay the Subordinate Obligations. Further, 
the City may pledge the revenues produced by a Separate Utility System to pay  the Bonds issued under this Master 
Ordinance by filing a written certificate of the Mayor and the Director of Finance and Administration declaring such 
pledge with the City and the Owner of the Bonds. 
Neither the Revenue nor Net Revenues may be pledged to the payment of any obligations of a Separate Utility System 
except that the Net Revenues may be pledged on a basis subordinate to the lien on such revenue to the lien of the Bonds.     
 10 
Additional Covenants 
The City has covenanted and agreed to and with the owners of record (the “Registered Owners”) of the Series 2022 Bonds 
and any Parity Bonds that the City will perform the following covenants: 
Rate Covenant.  The City has established, may from time to time revise, and shall maintain and shall collect from the 
users of the System, rates and charges for furnishing the services and the facilities of the System to such users thereof. 
Said rates and charges are, and shall continue to be, uniform as to all persons or properties which are of the same class. 
The City shall establish, maintain and collect such rates and charges for service of its System for so long as any Bonds 
are Outstanding and shall maintain the Rate Covenant. 
Acquire Projects.  The City shall commence the acquisition, construction and completion of any Project financed by 
proceeds of Bonds, and continue the same with all practical dispatch and in a sound and economical manner. 
Operate System.  The City shall operate the System in an efficient and economical manner and prescribe, revise, and 
collect such charges in connection therewith so that the services, facilities, and properties of the System may be furnished 
at the lowest possible cost consistent with sound economy and prudent management. 
Good Repair.  The City shal l operate, maintain, preserve, and keep the System and every part hereof in good repair, 
working order, and condition. 
Preserve Security.  The City shall preserve and protect the security of the Bonds and the rights of the Registered Owners 
thereof. 
Collect Revenues.  The City shall collect and hold in trust the Revenue of the System and other funds pledged to the 
payment of the Bonds and apply such Revenue of the System or other funds only as provided in the Master Ordinance 
and all series ordinances. 
Service Bonds.  The City shall pay and cause to be paid punctually the principal of and interest on Bonds on the date or 
dates, at the place or places, and in the manner that such sums are due in accordance with the Master Ordinance and all 
series ordinances. 
Pay Claims.  The City shall pay and discharge any and all lawful claims for labor, materials, and supplies which, if unpaid, 
might by law become a lien or charge upon the Revenue of the System, or any part of said Revenue of the System, or any 
funds in the hands of the Treasurer  or Director of Finance and Administration , prior or superior to the lien of the Bonds 
or which might impair the security of the Bonds to the end that the priority and security of the Bonds shall be fully 
preserved and protected. 
Encumbrances, Sales, or Transfers of the System:   The City shall not encumber, sell, lease, or dispose of the System or 
any part thereof, nor enter into any lease or agreement which would impair or impede the operation of the System or any 
part thereof necessary to secure adequate R evenue for the payment of the principal of and interest on the Bonds and for 
the City to meet the Rate Covenant, nor which would otherwise impair or impede the rights of the Registered Owners of 
the Bonds with respect to such Revenue or the operation of the System except as explicitly set forth in the Master 
Ordinance. See “Appendix B—Master Bond Ordinance and Series 2022 Ordinance.” 
Insurance.  The City shall self-insure or procure and keep in force insurance upon all buildings and structures of the 
System and the machinery and equipment therein, which are usually insured by entities operating like property, in good 
and responsible insurance companies. The amount of the insurance shall be such as may be required to adequately protect 
it and the Registered Owners of any Bonds from loss due to any casualty, and in the event of any such loss, the proceeds 
shall be used to repair or restore the System or for the payment of Bonds.  
 11 
Fidelity Bonds.  The City shall procure suitable fidelity bonds covering all of its officers and other employees charged 
with the operation of the System and the collection and disbursement of Revenue of the System. 
Engineers.  The City shall employ consulting engineers of acknowledged reputation, skill and experience in the 
improvement and operation of the System for any unusual or extraordinary items of maintenance, repair, extensions, or 
betterments as shall be required from time to time. All reports, estimates, and recommendations of such consulting 
engineers shall be filed with the Clerk and furnished to the Registered Owners of any Bonds upon request. 
Accounts.  The City shall keep proper and separate accounts and records in which complete and separate entries shall be 
made of all transactions relating to the System, and it will furnish complete operating and income statements upon request. 
Delinquencies.  The City shall not enter any new agreements or arrangements or make any new offers to provide System 
products or services at a discount from published rate schedules or provide free System products or services except: (i) 
for City-owned facilities, (ii) in case of emergencies, (iii) where the City exchanges services with other water systems, or 
(iv) where in the reasonable judgement of the City such action does not materially reduce the Revenue received by the 
City.  
Events of Default and Remedies 
See Section 18 “Events of Default” and Section 19 “Application of Funds and Moneys in Event of Default” in “Appendix 
B—Master Bond Ordinance and Series 2022 Ordinance” attached hereto.  
COVID-19 PANDEMIC  
State Response 
In response to evidence of community spread of COVID -19, on March 13, 2020, Idaho Governor Brad Little (the 
“Governor”) proclaimed a state of emergency throughout the State.  The State implemented a  phased plan for allowing 
economic activity to increase.  The plan occurred over four stages and set forth specific criteria for the State to meet before 
moving into each of the four stages, as well as business protocols for certain businesses to open in the various stages.  
COVID-19 vaccines are now available to all people in the State over the age of five. As of June 1, 2022, the State reports 
over 940,000 people are fully vaccinated with nearly half of those having received an additional booster dose. The State 
never issued vaccine mandates and banned vaccine passports.  
On March 8, 2022, the Governor announced that Idaho would end the health emergency declaration on April 15, 2022.  
There are currently no limitations on business operations, and no limits on gatherings.  
City Response 
The City and Water Renewal Services operated throughout the COVID -19 pandemic, making appropriate safety 
adjustments for employees based on guidance from the Center for Disease Control and the State. While there was a shift 
in flows, the overall total remaine d relatively the same throughout, and there was not a material, negative impact to the 
Revenue of the System. The City did not offer any delinquency forgiveness related to late payments, though local housing 
authorities were able to offer utility assistance to renters within the Service Area by way of funds the State received 
through the Emergency Rental Assistance program . Rather, collection rates of the System have  increased since March 
2020 and the City did not experience overall revenue loss as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic.  
While the City received Coronavirus Aid, Relief, and Economic Security Act funds and American Rescue Plan Act  
recovery funds, it did not allocate any of those funds to the System.   
Risk Factors 
The 
current domestic and international financial disruption has had, and may continue to have, negative repercussions 
upon state, national and global economies. Examples of potential impacts include volatility in the securities markets, 
significant losses in investment portfolios, a scarcity of credit, lack of confidence in the financial sector, reduced business  
 12 
activity, increased consumer bankruptcies, increased business failures and bankruptcies, and increased unemployment 
rates. 
The full impact of the C OVID-19 pandemic on the operations and financial condition of the City cannot be fully 
determined at this time due to the evolving nature of the pandemic, including uncertainties relating to the future actions 
of governmental authorities to contain or mitigate its impact, though such effect could be material and adverse.  The City 
is continuously monitoring the situation and will adjust its response in concert with federal, state and local health officials 
and governmental authorities.   
Effect on the Series 2022 Bonds 
The Series 2022 Bonds are secured by and payable from the Net Revenue of the System.  The Net Revenues are dependent 
upon payment of rates and charges. While COVID-19 pandemic has not thus far created a decrease in Net Revenues, the 
economic effects of COVID-19 may have adverse effects on the City’s overall collection of Revenue. 
 
CITY INDEBTEDNESS 
General  
The following is a description of statutory limitations on various types of debt authorized for municipalities in the State: 
Special Assessment Bonds.  Section 50-3101 et seq. and Section 50-1701 et seq. of the Idaho Code provid e for special 
assessment bonds for community infrastructure districts (“CID”) and local improvement districts (“LID”), respectively. 
There are no statutory limitations to the par amount of CID special assessment bonds that may be issued, other than that 
the amount assessed against any property within the district may not be more than the taxable value of the property.  For 
LID special assessment bonds, the aggregate fair market value of the real property within the assessment area, including 
the infrastructure to be financed with the special assessments, must be greater than three times the aggregate par amount 
of the LID special assessment bonds. 
Revenue Bonds.  There are no statutory limitations to the par amount of revenue bonds that can be issued by a municipality 
or CID, provided that the par amount cannot exceed the costs of the project to be financed with proceeds of the revenue 
bonds.  The project must be self-supporting and in the case of new money bonds, the par amount cannot exceed the amount 
authorized by voter approval or judicial confirmation. In the event of refunding bonds, the par amount cannot exceed the 
par amount of the refunded bonds; as such, the portion of proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds allocated to the refunding of 
the Refunded Bonds cannot exceed the par amount of the Refunded Bonds. 
General Obligation Debt .  Section  50-1019 of the Idaho Code limits voter -approved general obligation debt for cities 
located in the State to an amount not to exceed 2 percent of the market value for assessment purposes, less the aggregate 
outstanding voter-approved general obligation bond indebtedness. General obligation debt requires two-thirds (2/3) voter 
approval.  CIDs can also issue general obligation debt, but the aggregate outstanding par amount of the general obligation 
bonds, together with any other debt of the CID, may not exceed 9% of the actual or adjusted market value on all taxable 
property within the CID. 
Certificates of Participation.  Certificates of participation represent undivided ownership interests in lease payments under 
financing leases entered into by a municipality.  The payments evidenced by the lease are special obligations of the 
municipality subject to annual appropriation of the lease payments, and not a general obligation of the municipality.  These 
obligations are subject to a municipality’s willingness and ability to budget and annually appropriate funding to make the 
payments.  Municipalities are authorized to lease real property pursuant to chapter 14, Title 50, Idaho Code.

Future Financings 
Upon issuance of the Series 2022 Bonds, the City will have  approximately $490,000,000 of the Bonding Capacity 
remaining to be issued and secured by the Net Revenues of the System. At the time of issuance, the Series 2022 Bonds 
will be the only outstanding debt secured by a pledge of Net Revenues. The City intends to enter into the WIFIA Loan in 
the near future, the proceeds of which will be  used to finance a portion of the Project.   See “P URPOSE AND USE OF 
PROCEEDS – Project – Additional Funding for Project” above.  The Capital Improvement Plan also contemplates 
additional Parity Bonds being issued in the next 3 years. See “THE SYSTEM – Capital Improvement Plan” below.

THE SYSTEM 
Introduction 
Pursuant to the authority under Section 50-323, Idaho Code, the  City owns and manages a public water renewal (sewer) 
utility, including the collection and treatment (the “System”). The System is separate from the private water utility serving 
the City, and is operated by Water Renewal Services (“WRS”) within the City’s Public Works Department.  The System 
is responsible for collecting and renewing used water (sewer) within the City. WRS oversees approximately $2 billion in 
assets to renew more than 10 billion gallons of used water per year. 
General and Service Area 
The System service area is 163 square miles and includes the City of Boise, Garden City, Eagle Sewer District and West 
Boise Sewer District (the “Service Area”). The Service Area is outlined in the map below. 
 
  
 
 16 
Population Served. The City provides service to approximately 90,000 accounts, 93% of which are residential. The System 
serves a total population of greater than 285,000. The City’s accounts are divided into the following four classes: (1) 
residential, (2) commercial unmonitored, (3) commercial monitored, and (4) wholesale.  
Residential and commercial unmonitored accounts have relatively consistent flow and loads and are considered 
“unmonitored” customers because their effluent volume  and strength are generally common and predictable. These two 
classifications make up approximately 95% of all the City’s accounts , and account for approximately 83% of total 
Revenue.  
Commercial monitored and wholesale accounts have effluent with the potential to create an upset or require rapid process 
changes at the water renewal facility in order to treat it. The following table reflects the top ten accounts of the System , 
the customer class, the percentage of overall flow, and the percentage of rate revenues. 
Top Ten  
Water Renewal Customers (2021) 
 
           Source: The City of Boise. 
(1) Mircon Technology, Inc. is an American founded producer of computer memory and computer data storage , founded in 1976, 
based in Boise, Idaho, with currently over 43,000 employees in 17 different countries.   
Wholesale Accounts. The City is currently under long term contracts to accept  used water from the Eagle Sewer District  
(the “ESD”), West Boise Sewer District (the “WBSD”), and Garden City (“GC”). These three “wholesale” accounts each 
own, operate and maintain their own collection systems, which convey used water flow to a point of connection with the 
City’s collection system. Each connection point is monitored and results are used to determine respective service fees. 
The following tables provides the breakdown between residential and commercial accounts for the ESD, WBSD, and GC.  
Wholesale Accounts

capacity connection fees, along with maximum allowed buildout capacity. All treatment costs are allocated 
proportionately based on total flow and constituent loadings. Each agreement requires that the sewer district or city abide

by all national pretreatment standards. The agreements with ESD and GS are perpetual and the City does not expect either 
party to make changes thereto.  
The City’s agreement with the WBSD terminates in 2026, and the City and WBSD have begun discussions related to the 
end of the agreement. The City anticipates that the wholesale agreement will not be renewed and that the City will directly 
serve the current WBSD customers. If the agreement with WBSD is terminated, the City will add approximately 6,000 
new accounts. Though the City already services those customers, termination of the agreement with WBSD will allow 
the City to adjust rates. Rates and fees assessed to the City’s wholesale accounts lag behind those assessed to residential, 
commercial monitored and commercial unmonitored accounts due to older methods of calculation. As such, the City 
believes termination will be financially beneficial for the System.  
The City’s expectation regarding new accounts is based on the WBSD’s options for treatment of its own used water. After 
termination of the wholesale agreement with the City, the WBSD could build its own treatment facility or pursue 
connection with a neighboring munic ipality. The City estimates that neither of these options present practical economic 
alternatives for the WBSD at this time. However, in the event the WBSD provides an alternative treatment system for the 
WBSD’s customers, the City does not view such alternative as economically detrimental given any potential reduction in 
rate revenue would likely be offset by a corresponding reduction in costs.  
Collection System   
Water Renewal Services has a program to inspect and track all of its collection system assets on a regular schedule. The 
condition assessment program, combined with flow projections, provides the City with information needed to rehabilitate 
degrading pipes and plan for growth in a timely manner.  
The City’s collection system includes over 900 miles of collection system pipeline and 28 lift stations that lift the sewage 
collected in low-lying areas to higher gravity collection pipers (the “Collection System”). Most of the Collection System 
was constructed within the last 30 years and is in good condition. Inspections and asset tracking have allowed the City to 
operate efficient repair and rehabilitation. Current estimates put approximately 1% of the total collection system in less 
than desirable condition. The following table sets forth the details of the Collection System:  
 
Component Total 
Small diameter  (<21 inches) gravity sewer pipe 825 miles 
Large diameter  (21-72 inches) gravity sewer pipe 84 miles 
Pressure sewer pipe 14 miles 
Manholes >22,000 
Service connections >78,000 
Lift stations 28 
      Source: The City of Boise. 
There are two diversions, or structures, within the Collection System that the City uses to manage flow distribution 
between the Lander Street water renewal facility ( the “Lander WRF”) and the West Boise water ren ewal facility (the 
“West Boise WRF”): Americana diversion and Lander Street diversion. The City has been using both diversions to send 
more flow to the West Boise WRF and less to the Lander WRF. As of 2020, however,  the Americana diversion is not in 
use due to its condition. In accordance with the City’s asset management plan,  the City will either improve the Lander 
Street diversion or rehab the Americana diversion by 2030.  See “P
URPOSE AND USE OF PROCEEDS – Project” and “THE 
SYSTEM – Capital Improvement Plan” below.  
Treatment System   
Lander Street Water Renewal Facility .  The Lander WRF was constructed in 1948 and is a secondary treatment water 
renewal facility located in Boise along the north bank of the Boise River. The Lander WRF is a conventional aerated 
activated sludge secondary treatment facility designed for biological nutrient removal. The facility currently renews used  
 18 
water by removing both nitrogen and phosphorus in the biological process. Upgrades to the headworks and ultraviolet 
treatment facilities are currently under construction and scheduled to be online in 2022.  
The capacity of a water renewal facility is defined by hydraulic and treatment capacities, which are essentially its ability 
to physically hold all incoming flow and treat it to the standards defined in the City’s National Pollutant Discharge 
Elimination System permits. See “THE SYSTEM–Regulatory Environment and Permits” below. 
Hydraulic Capacity. The hydraulic constriction associated with the intermediate pump station is the only near -
term limitation for the Lander WRF. The City is aware of the limitation and can use the Lander Street diversion 
to reduce flow if necessary.  
Treatment Capacity. The Lan der WRF’s treatment capacity is mainly limited by a combination of biological 
oxygen demand (“BOD”) loading and the ammonia effluent limitation. The ammonia permit regulation forces the 
WRF to operate at a long solids retention time, which generates a large volume of biomass due to the BOD load, 
causing the capacity limitation in the secondary clarifiers.  
Flow Capacity and Projections.  The Lan der WRF has current capacity to renew an average of 13.1 mgd. The 
City anticipates the Lander WRF will require capacity to renew an average of 17 mgd by 2030.  
The City completed risk assessments and developed a plan for replacement of most major Lander WRF components. 
Impr
ovements have been prioritized based on several considerations. Phase one components, deemed the most urgent,  
include headworks and ultraviolet disinfection, and are estimated to be complete in Summer 2022. The City expects to 
fund these improvements with Rate-Funded Capital. Phase two components include primary and secondary clarifiers and 
planning for those improvements has begun, and the City anticipates that proceeds of the Series 2022 Bonds will finance 
all or a portion of phase two. Improvements to Lander WRF will not only replace aged assets, but will add capacity and 
ensure regulatory compliance.  
West Boise Water Renewal Facility. The West Boise WRF was commissioned in 1976 and provides advanced secondary 
treatment with ammonia and phosphorus removal. All renewed water is disinfected with u ltraviolet disinfection, then 
discharged to the south channel of the Boise River. In 2015, the City upgraded the West Boise WRF to an enhanced 
biological phosphorus removal process, aided by primary sludge fermentation. It has also been recovering struvite  from 
a recycle stream to sell on the commercial market.  
The West Boise WRF is currently rated by its NPDES permit for a design flow of 24 mgd annual average month flow. 
The facility is operated by nitrification mode to meet water quality standards and ef fluent toxicity requirements. The 
recent growth in the City has contributed to the increase in total flow to the West Boise WRF. 
Hydraulic Capacity. Th
 e hydraulic capacity of key unit processes at the West Boise WRF are not projected to 
meet limits given the peak monthly flow projections at buildout.   
Treatment Capacity. The seco ndary process is designated as currently limited. The aeration basin volume is 
insufficient to meet the target regulatory condition under current operating strategy. A secondary treatment 
expansion is required a t the West Boise WRF to meet the 203 0 target condition with the expected flows and 
loading to the facility. The next limiting processes will be digesters and belt filter press capacity, but these are not 
as imminent as the aeration basin capacity constraints. 
Flow Capacity and Projections. The We
 st Boise WRF has current capacity to renew an average of 22.8 mgd. The 
City anticipates the West Boise WRF will require capacity to renew an average of 25.5 mgd by 2030. 
The Project and the City’s CIP are designed to meet the City’s anticipated average peak monthl y flow projections through 
2030. In addition to the Lander WRF and West Boise WRF improvements noted above, t he Project and CIP include 
construction of one new WRF. The additional WRF is projected to renew an average of 5 mgd by 2030.  
 19 
Flow Capacity and Projections 
  
Phosphorus Removal Facility. The Phosphorus Removal Facility (the “PRF”) is a water renewal facility that removes 
non-point source total phosphorus pollution from an agricultural drain that discharges to the Boise River. The PRF is a 
unique pollutant offset facility that removes more total phosphorus from the watershed than would be removed by only 
upgrading the existing water renewal facility.  
Twenty Mile South Biosolids Application Site. The Twenty Mile South Biosolids Application Site (“Biosolids Site”) is a 
4,225-acre farm that receives biosolids settled from the primary and secondary clarifiers generated at the Lander WRF 
and West Boise WRF. After the biosolids are dewatered at the water renewal facilities, they are trucked to the Biosolids 
Site and stored for up to two years. The  biosolids are applied to fields of forage crops, which are ultimately sold to local 
farmers.  
Water Renewal Utility Plan. The Water Renewal Utility Plan (the “Plan”)  represents a significant evolution in resourc e 
management for the City. The Plan seeks to shift the utility’s focus from simply disposing byproducts and complying with 
state and federal requirements to managing, recovering, and reusing resources. The Plan also (i) establishes a strategy for 
Water Renewal Services to meet the needs of the City, including the expected flow increase of nearly 20% over the next 
20 years, (ii) addresses pressures of climate change, and (iii) plans for necessary improvements, as well as the financial 
outlay associated therewith.  
Capital Improvement Plan  
The City has developed a ten-year capital improvement plan (the “CIP”) to provide approximately $979 million of needed 
capital improvements to the System for Fiscal Year 2022 through Fiscal Year 2032 , excluding any financing costs, 
capitalized interest, or reserve funding associated with the Series 2022 Bonds or any future financings .  The Project 
represents expenditures of approximately $815  million or approximately 83% of the CIP.   See “P
URPOSE AND USE OF 
PROCEEDS – Project” above. 
In addition to those improvements comprising the Project, the CIP currently includes completion upgrades to the Lander 
Street WRF, smaller education, environmental, and WRF office upgrade projects, collection line extensions, future design 
projects, and repair and maintenance projects. Further detail is provided in the table below.

Water Renewal Services Rates   
Monthly Rates.  Historically, rates are considered annually as part of the City’s annual budget development process.  The 
City of Boise City Council (“City Council”) has final approval of the rates of the System. Rates are usually approved in 
June or July for implementation at  the start of the following Fiscal Year, on October 1. City Council may adjust rates at 
other times during a Fiscal Year by approval of an ordinance after three readings.  
A 5-year history of water renewal services rate adjustments is presented in the following table: 
 
Historical Water Renewal Services Rate Adjustments 
 
 
Source: The City of Boise. 
CCF = Hundred cubic feet of potable water = 748 gallons. 
(1) The Overall Increase is the amount that rate revenue increased as a whole but individual customer categories vary to achieve the overall 
annual increase. 
(2) Base charge is assessed to each monthly bill for residential and commercial customers in addition to usage charges. 
(3) Residential usage charges for each month are based upon the previous year's observed winter average water demand in CCF multiplied 
by the price per CCF.  
(4) Commercial unmonitored usage charges for each month are based upon the previous year's observed winter average water demand i n 
CCF multiplied by the price per CCF of the Strength Category (SC) that best matches the amount of contamination discharged in each 
customer's used water. 
(5) Commercial monitored usage is based upon a customer's actual monthly measured usage and constituents which are applied to the  
appropriated prices per gallon of flow or loadings as shown in the table above.  
Approximately 25% of the revenue from the City’s residential customers has historically been generated from the base 
charge associated with such accounts, and approximately 75% from the usage charge. 
The City is conducting a Cost of Service Study and Rate Design for Fiscal Year 2023 to determine the adequacy of the 
existing rates, which will take into account the funding required to maintain and upgrade the Syst em in accordance with 
the Capital Improvement Plan. See “T
HE SYSTEM – Capital Improvement Plan” above.   The City plans to annually 
increase rates, subject to annual City Council approval, to keep pace with increasing System and improvement costs. The 
City estimates that the System’s rate revenue must increase approximately 9.9% over each of the next four years. The rate 
increase to each customer classification may be higher or lower, so long as the overall 9.9% rate increase is achieved.

Billing and Collection.  The City bills residential and commercial unmonitored accounts using average winter water usage. 
Commercial unmonitored customers receive a monthly bill , while residential customers are billed bi -monthly. Charges 
vary based on the strength of used-water typical to the discharger. Commercial monitored accounts are billed each month 
based on their measured average daily flows and constitute loads, and wholesale accounts are billed according to their 
respective agreement. See “Wholesale Accounts” above.  
Accounts with past due balances are charged 1.5% monthly interest. Past due accounts are initially collected directly by 
City employees. The City utilizes letters, phone calls, credit bureau reporting, and service shut-off. Escalated past -due 
accounts are passed to the City’s legal department for small claims court or to a third party collection agency.  
The City may terminate service in the following circumstances: (1) failure to pay service fees, (2) failure to abide by the 
terms of a water renewal services fee payment arrangement, (3) misrepresentation of identity of the user receiving service, 
(4) connection to the System without knowledge or approval of the City, or (5) failure to comply with the provisions of 
City Code.

The Water Renewal Fund 
The operations of the System are accounted for in the Water Renewal Fund, which is categorized as an enterprise fund of 
the City.  All operations, debt service, and capital improvements to the System are accounted for in the Water Renewal 
Fund. 
The City includes in its annual budget for the System estimated receipts of revenues for services, fees and other funds to 
cover all expenditures, including expenses of operation and maintenance, repair and replacement of facilities and 
equipment of the System.  The Fiscal Year 2022 budget reflects revenues and expenditures totaling $73,859,486 and 
$60,538,619, respectively.  
Financial Reports 
The following are summaries of the City’s Water Renewal Fund Statement of Net Position and Statement of Revenues, 
Expenditures and Changes in Fund Net Position as extracted from the City’s audited financial statements for the years 
indicated.  
The summary of Statement of Revenues, Expenditures and Changes in Fund Net Position also includes projected numbers 
for Fiscal Year 2022. The City has prepared unaudited f inancial statements for Fiscal Year 2022 based upon quarterly 
updates through April 2022 and projections estimated through the end of Fiscal Year 2022.  The City expects the trends 
reflected therein to continue for the twelve-month period ended September  30, 2022, as there are no material changes 
expected in Fiscal Year 2022. Although the City believes the unaudited results are accurate and expects the trend to 
continue through the Fiscal Year end, the City’s actual year-end results could differ based on a number of factors, 
including factors affecting the year -end results occurring  in the month of September  2022, typical adjustments to year -
end results during the course of the outside audit, and other factors.  Inclusion of unaudited results of the Water Renewal 
Fund herein is not a representation by the City of a year-end result.   
The projections in this Official Statement are based on a range of assumptions that the City believes to be 
reasonable.  Because of the nature of projections, including variability in assumptions, economic conditions and changes 
in the regulatory environment, the City cannot guarantee those results.   Potential investors should not rely on the 
projections as statements of fact.  Such projections are subject to change and will change, from time to time.  As a result, 
projected results may not be realized and actual results could be significantly higher or lower than projected.  The City is 
not obligated to update, or otherwise revise, the financial projections or the specific portions  presented to reflect  
circumstances existing after the date when made or to reflect the occurrence of future events, even in the event that any 
or all of the assumptions are shown to be in error.

OPEB contributions are included in personnel costs, the City does not forecast growth in pension and OPEB liabilities alongside growth 
in personnel.  Additional costs of operating new facilities, including some personnel costs, are included in the O&M  Expenses line from 
FY2026 and beyond. 
(7) After FY2023, O&M expenses increase annually by 1.15% accounting for increasing costs of materials, chemicals, supplies, etc.  As new 
facilities are completed, additional O&M costs are added to the rate projection.

Revenue Bonds, and estimated debt service payments on a future WIFIA  Loan.  The voted authorization for the two revenue bonds plus 
WIFIA loan is $570M to be issued between FY2022 and FY2031.   
(10) Total Rate-Funded Capital is the portion of annual capital expenses that will be funded directly with Net Revenues available after debt 
service has been paid.  The remainder of the annual capital expenses will be funded through bond or WIFIA loan proceeds.

Parity Bond Debt Service Expectation 
The City expects that annual debt service will continue to increase after Fiscal Year 2027.  The majority of the WIFIA 
Loan draws will occur in Fiscal Years 2027 through 2031 to provide funds to complete the Project . See “THE SYSTEM – 
Capital Improvement Plan.” Prior to drawing funds on the WIFIA Loan or issuing other additional Parity Bonds, the City 
will be required to meet the covenants for Parity Bonds included in the Master Ordinance; see “SECURITY FOR THE 
SERIES 2022 BONDS – Future Obligations.” The City expects to begin amortization of all Parity Bonds related to the 
Project in Fiscal Year 2032. Current projections for annual debt service on Parity Bonds following completion of the 
Project is $33.15 million, beginning in Fiscal Year 2032.  
Regulatory Environment and Permits 
Operation of the System is regulated by the United States Environmental Protection Agency (“EPA”), which approved 
the State’s request for a state operated pollutant discharge elimination system in June 2018, thereby creating the Idaho 
Pollution Discharge Elimination System (“IPDES”) and transferring permitting authority to the State. While the State 
took over the IPDES permitting authority from the EPA, the City’s current permits are still under the federal National 
Pollutant Discharge Elimination System (“NPDES”) program. The City has two existing NPDES permits for its West 
Boise and Lander Street water renewal facilities which were issued in 2012 and expired on July 31, 2017. The City 
reapplied and has been operating both water renewal facilities under  an administrative extension while it awaits the 
issuance of the next permits. The City has received and is reviewing the new preliminary draft permit and expects it to be 
finalized in Summer 2022 (the “Updated IPDES Permit”).  
The Plan identifies that future IPDES permits may modify their current permit requirements by placing possible limits on 
total phosphorous ( “TP”), ammonia, BOD/total suspended solids ( “TSS”) removal rates, temperature, and emerging 
constituents and the Project is designed to address these issues. The City is working with  the Idaho Department of 
Environmental Quality (“IDEQ”) to develop a total combined mass loading approach for TP discharges to the lower Boise 
River, which would provide a limit for all facilities combined rather than limits for each individual facility. Ammonia 
limits under new IPDES permits are expected to be less stringent than the current limits, but not high enough to affect 
operations. BOD/TSS removal rates are expected to remain the same, with a changed methodology to match current 
permitting standards. The City is also working with IDEQ to set temperature limits on discharges into the Boise River 
through the use of thermal variances authorized under the Clean Water Act in order to produce better environmental 
outcomes. Finally, the City does not expect emerging constituents to be included in the new permits, but is taking a 
proactive approach to control emerging constituents and provide source reduction in light of the current focus on emerging 
constituents in the wastewater industry. See “P
URPOSE AND USE OF PROCEEDS—Project” above. 
The City is in compliance with all State and Federal acts, permits and regulations. There are no pending administrative 
actions by any regulatory agencies involving the City’s System.  The System remains in compliance with all appl icable 
parameters at this time. The Updated IPDES Permit will reflect current Clean Water Act requirements and associated 
State standards. For any constituent regulations the City cannot immediately comply with, the Updated IPDES Permit 
will include a schedule of compliance to allow time to come into compliance.  
THE CITY 
General 
The City of Boise City, Idaho, organized in 1866 in accordance with Article 12, Section 1 and Article 18, Section 6 of the 
Idaho Constitution, is located in the Southwest portion of Idaho in Ada County (the “County”) and serves as the Idaho 
State Capital.  Idaho ranks first nationally in percentage of population growth from 2019 to 2020 according to initial 2020 
Census data from the U.S. Census Bureau.  The City is the largest municipality in Idaho and has an estimated population 
of 239,879 as of January 2022.  The City is the principal business and government center of the State. The City is governed 
by a Mayor and a six-member City Council. 
Mayor – Council System 
The City operates under the mayor-council system of government as a city of the first class under the general laws of the 
State with a mayor (the “Mayor”) and six council members (the “City Council”).  The Mayor is elected to a four -year  
 30 
term and serves as the chief executive officer for the City, responsible for carrying out policies set by the City Council 
and for enforcing the City Code. Prior to legislation passed in 2020, City Council members (“Council Members”) were 
also elected for four-year terms, three being elected every two years to stagger the terms for continuity.  
Section 50-707A, Idaho Code, was amended to require cities with populations  greater than 100,000 people to establish 
districts for city counc il elections  and elect Council Members by such districts. The City created six  districts and 
conducted the scheduled 2021 City Council election in accordance with the legislation , appointing three new Council 
Members for two-year terms. In 2023, all Council Members will be up for reelection, at which time the odd-numbered  
districts will run for four -year terms and even-numbered district will run for two years, i n order to reestablish staggered 
terms for continuity.  
The following are the current members of the City Council:
